This initiative marks the second RO project in Argentina, supporting sustainable waste management and helping the country work toward the\nGlobal Methane Pledge\ngoal of reducing methane emissions by 30% by 2030.\nRead the Spanish version of the story here!\nArgentina is also part of RO\u2019s\nCommunity of Practice\non Reducing Methane Emissions from Organic Sources in Latin America and the Caribbean (CoP Met-LAC)\n,\nco-led with the\nLEDS LAC Platform\n. This new project complements previous RO work done in the region with neighboring countries featured in the initial\nReciclo Org\u00e1nicos Latin America\nProgram. Both the CoP Met-LAC initiative and the original RO program received support from the\nGlobal Methane Hub (GMH)\n.\nThrough 2026, this project will assist the Argentine government in creating a framework for improving the management of organic waste treatment byproducts, including compost, digestate and biogas. Collaborating with a broad network of stakeholders\u2014ranging from farmers to government and municipal officials\u2014the RO team, led by\nCCAP\nand\nImplementaSur\n, will showcase the potential for reducing methane and carbon emissions by\nintegrating compos...",

However, the waste generation in modern cities present several new features that affect the MSW system. These new features include both positive aspects, such as innovative recycling techniques and increased public environmental awareness, as well as challenging aspects, including a rise in the amount of waste generated and in the complexityof waste composition. As a result, MSW systems have to adapt to new opportunities and threats offer by the context by exploiting their strong and weak points. In this line, this article conducts a comprehensive review of contemporary material and waste flows, followed by a revision of the current state of the MSW systems in Argentina and a particular analysis of an Argentinean case study using SWOT (StrengthsWeaknesses-Opportunities-Threats) methodology. Some features of this site may not work without it.\nINFORMACI\u00d3N GENERAL\nRESUMEN\nESTADISTICAS\nEvento\nMunicipal Solid waste management systems: application of SWOT methodology to analyze an Argentinean case study\nRossit, Diego Gabriel\n;\nNesmachnow, Sergio\n;\nCavallin, Antonella\nTipo del evento:\nConferencia\nNombre del evento:\nVI Iberoamerican Congress on Smart Cities (ICSC-CITIES 2023)\nFecha del evento:\n13/11/2023\nInstituci\u00f3n Organizadora:\nUniversidad Aut\u00f3noma del Estado de Morelos;\nT\u00edtulo del Libro:\nProceedings of the VI Iberoamerican Congress on Smart Cities (ICSC-CITIES 2023)\nEditorial:\nUniversidad Aut\u00f3noma del Estado de Morelos\nISBN:\n978-607-99960-1-7\nIdioma:\nIngl\u00e9s\nClasificaci\u00f3n tem\u00e1tica:\nOtras Ingenier\u00edas y Tecnolog\u00edas\nResumen\nHistorically, Municipal Solid Waste (MSW) systems emerged in response to society\u2019s needs for managing manufacturing and consumption waste. However, the waste generation in modern cities present several new features that affect the MSW system. These new features include both positive aspects, such as innovative recycling techniques and increased public environmental awareness, as well as challenging aspects, including a rise in the amount of waste generated and in the complexityof waste composition. As a result, MSW systems have to adapt to new opportunities and threats offer by the context by exploiting their strong and weak points. In this line, this article conducts a comprehensive review of contemporary material and waste flows, followed by a revision of the current state of the MSW systems in Argentina and a particular analysis of an Argentinean case study using SWOT (StrengthsWeaknesses-Opportunities-Threats) methodology. The findings of this analysis highligh...",

  "snippet_or_summary": "top of page\nHome\nAbout\nAbout Us\nOur Team\nPartners\nBoard\nCareers\nOur Work\nPrograms\nRegions\nEvents\nNews\nSubscribe\nPress Releases\nBlog\nMedia Resources\nMore\nUse tab to navigate through the menu items.\nDonate\nAll Posts\nEvents\nBlog\nInsights\nPress releases\nCOP\nRecycle Organics\nOp-Eds\nSearch\nNew Collaboration Advances Organic Waste Recovery in Argentina to Reduce Greenhouse Gas Emissions\nCCAP\nApr 24\n6 min read\nRecycle Organics partners with CCAC to combat short lived climate pollutants (SLCPs) in Argentina.\nWASHINGTON, D.C. \u2013\nThe\nRecycle Organics (RO) Program\nis expanding its efforts to tackle methane emissions in the Global South through a new project with the\nClimate and Clean Air Coalition (CCAC)\n. This collaboration aims to address short-lived climate pollutants (SLCPs) in Argentina by developing policies for organic waste recovery. This initiative marks the second RO project in Argentina, supporting sustainable waste management and helping the country work toward the\nGlobal Methane Pledge\ngoal of reducing methane emissions by 30% by 2030.\nRead the Spanish version of the story here!\nArgentina is also part of RO\u2019s\nCommunity of Practice\non Reducing Methane Emissions from Organic Sources in Latin America and the Caribbean (CoP Met-LAC)\n,\nco-led with the\nLEDS LAC Platform\n. This new project complements previous RO work done in the region with neighboring countries featured in the initial\nReciclo Org\u00e1nicos Latin America\nProgram. Both the CoP Met-LAC initiative and the original RO program received support from the\nGlobal Methane Hub (GMH)\n.\nThrough 2026, this project will assist the Argentine government in creating a framework for improving the management of organic waste treatment byproducts, including compost, digestate and biogas. Collaborating with a broad network of stakeholders\u2014ranging from farmers to government and municipal officials\u2014the RO team, led by\nCCAP\nand\nImplementaSur\n, will showcase the potential for reducing methane and carbon emissions by\nintegrating compos...",

It is a \nleading food producer with large -scale agricultural and livestock \nindustries.  \nThe historical volatility of economic growth and the accumulat ion \nof institutional obstacles have negatively affected the country\u2019s \ndevelopment. A turning point in economic policies came in 2020 as a result of the change in government and the COVID -\n19 outbreak. As a response, Argentina has implemented fiscal, monetar y and exchange rate policies designed to support \nthe social and productive sectors. As Winston Churchill put it: \u201cNever let a good crisis go to waste \u201d. However, the waste generation in modern cities present several new features that affect the MSW system. These new features include both positive aspects, such as innovative recycling techniques and increased public environmental awareness, as well as challenging aspects, including a rise in the amount of waste generated and in the complexityof waste composition. As a result, MSW systems have to adapt to new opportunities and threats offer by the context by exploiting their strong and weak points. In this line, this article conducts a comprehensive review of contemporary material and waste flows, followed by a revision of the current state of the MSW systems in Argentina and a particular analysis of an Argentinean case study using SWOT (StrengthsWeaknesses-Opportunities-Threats) methodology. Some features of this site may not work without it.\nINFORMACI\u00d3N GENERAL\nRESUMEN\nESTADISTICAS\nEvento\nMunicipal Solid waste management systems: application of SWOT methodology to analyze an Argentinean case study\nRossit, Diego Gabriel\n;\nNesmachnow, Sergio\n;\nCavallin, Antonella\nTipo del evento:\nConferencia\nNombre del evento:\nVI Iberoamerican Congress on Smart Cities (ICSC-CITIES 2023)\nFecha del evento:\n13/11/2023\nInstituci\u00f3n Organizadora:\nUniversidad Aut\u00f3noma del Estado de Morelos;\nT\u00edtulo del Libro:\nProceedings of the VI Iberoamerican Congress on Smart Cities (ICSC-CITIES 2023)\nEditorial:\nUniversidad Aut\u00f3noma del Estado de Morelos\nISBN:\n978-607-99960-1-7\nIdioma:\nIngl\u00e9s\nClasificaci\u00f3n tem\u00e1tica:\nOtras Ingenier\u00edas y Tecnolog\u00edas\nResumen\nHistorically, Municipal Solid Waste (MSW) systems emerged in response to society\u2019s needs for managing manufacturing and consumption waste. However, the waste generation in modern cities present several new features that affect the MSW system. These new features include both positive aspects, such as innovative recycling techniques and increased public environmental awareness, as well as challenging aspects, including a rise in the amount of waste generated and in the complexityof waste composition. As a result, MSW systems have to adapt to new opportunities and threats offer by the context by exploiting their strong and weak points. In this line, this article conducts a comprehensive review of contemporary material and waste flows, followed by a revision of the current state of the MSW systems in Argentina and a particular analysis of an Argentinean case study using SWOT (StrengthsWeaknesses-Opportunities-Threats) methodology. The findings of this analysis highligh...",
